Great experience! Extremely nice staff in Downtown Disney. No transfer fee from northern California to this location during the Thanksgiving rush!

It would have been extremely hard to find if I hadn't done a lot of research before hand. I am writing this review to help others find the location. The staff explained to me that Disney does not allow them to put any signs to find the parking lot. You have to enter off of Disneyland Drive. I came in from the south off of Katella. It is the first light with a road sign that says Paradise Pier with an arrow to the left. Just tell the cast member at the guard shack that you are there to drop off a car and he will let you through. They will open up the gate just passed the guard shack on the right where you drop the car. You park in the lot directly south of the AMC Theatre.<//review>

<text>I had an extremely disappointing experience with this specific Alamo Branch.  I rented a car from Alamo in Monterrey, CA to drive to Anaheim.  I specifically selected Alamo because they provided after hours drop off.  I arrived in Anaheim at approximately 9:00 P.M. and used my GPS to locate the Alamo Rent A Car building.  I kept driving down Disneyland Dr. looking for any signs of the Alamo building.  My GPS kept saying I had arrived but there were no signs of the building.  This was an extremely difficult drive since it was late, I was unfamiliar with the area, and the park was starting to empty creating a ton of pedestrians.  After approximately 45 minutes of driving up and down the road I finally found a Disney employee who had a better idea of where I could find the Alamo building.  (It was not at the address given according to GPS.  I later learned the building uses one generic address that does not correlate to a specific location.)  I drove all around the area the Disney Employee directed me to, but still I saw no sign of the Alamo building.  The location was now filled with pedestrians and this created a very dangerous driving situation.
After 30 more minutes of driving around in circles, I located a security guard on bicycle.  He told me that it is not possible to actually see the Alamo building while driving.  You must in fact park the car and walk around the edge of the AMC theatre to find the Alamo building.  I asked him to explain exactly where I should park and thanked him for his assistance.  I drove to the unmarked parking lot.  (It's actually marked as the Grand Californian Overflow Parking lot.  No mention of Alamo Rent a Car)  I drove to both possible entrances, but sure enough they were both gated and inaccessible.  I drove around for another 20 minutes until I found the bicycle security guard, who shockingly was speaking to another car who also couldn't find the Alamo drop zone.  I told him of the problem with the gates.  This non Alamo employee (No actual Alamo employee was available to assist me.) was extremely helpful and about 15 minutes later got the gate open for me.  I parked in a random spot in this large parking lot.  There were no designated spots for car return.  I got out of the car and followed the security guard who led me to the building and dropped off the keys.
All in all without any exaggeration, it took me at least 2 hours to drop off my car.  While I consider myself a good driver I made many illegal driving turns while searching aimlessly for the building and getting myself stuck on dead-ends.  I was forced to make three point turns in a poorly lit area with tremendous foot traffic leading to a dangerous situation for me and the many families heading home from the park.
The next day I walked to voice my concerns with the Alamo employee.  He basically laughed when I brought up my issues, stating "People complain about the after hours drop off everyday, I've told the manager but he doesn't do anything.  Maybe if you complain he might listen and have something done."
This experience was inexcusable.  A major problem exists, and the business is aware of it, yet refuses to take action, leading to customer frustration, and dangerous conditions for both customers and pedestrians.<//text><date>1439038631699<//date><GmapID>0x80dcd7d88817341b:0x1bfb71dc45933a46</GmapID>< user_id>

< Text>
We requested a vehicle that would hold 5 people and luggage.  We Got a lovely GMC SUV that was immaculately clean and was perfect for all of us.  It sat 6 very comfortably but we lowered one of the back row seats to be able to get all our luggage.  The two grandchildren, 5 and 8, fought about seating alone in the back row so we had them take turns.  And I had my very own comfy seat without being squished between two car seats in the back seat.

We picked it up at Disneyland which was so convenient; we just walked to the Alamo office in Downtown Disney, were helped by a very nice and funny gentleman and then we just drove it to our hotel.

We delivered the car at the Oakland Airport after visiting Universal,  Santa Rosa and Napa, CA.

The best thing about the whole deal was that it was the best price we got after many calls to different car rentals.  We went thru Costco and saved about 50% from other companies.  We will rent from them again.

Happy Abuelita!</Text>

<review>Having visited America in larger groups numerous times and this being our last night in SF we expected to enjoy a lovely meal before leaving for England. From the very beginning we were treated badly. We were put on tables outside which should have been absolutely fine as they offered us the outdoor heaters but even this was too complex for them. The manager Lauris was very standoffish, neglected us and had a bad attitude when asked politely for condiments etc. He upsold orders to a cringeworthy degree. The main problem was the 2 card maximum payment policy. We were on the last night of a 3 week trip across 3 states as a group of 7 and hadn't come across this policy and service this poor for such average food. <Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
I've been all around California (and the rest the U.S.); this is still the best menudo I can find.

First thing -- most important -- Rosa Maria's restaurant only serves their menudo on the weekend; this is one of the main ways to tell if a business prepares their menudo fresh or simply reheats a frozen stock.

The tripe used is the reticulum section, or "honeycomb", the best type of meat for the stew -- no grease, no gristle. They boil away the fat, ensuring the meat and stock aren't oily and clouded, add the most tender hominy and give it the time it requires to properly stew.

By the time it makes its way to you, this menudo's been properly seasoned and the additional spices and trimmings the staff provide simply make an already amazing dish even more mouthwatering. To top it all off, they'll even add a meaty, tender pork bone, the perfect way to finish off such a satisfying meal.

This place is excellent. Sometimes, the beans have little rocks, but that's just another sign of freshness.

Keep it up, Rosa Maria's! I'll see you next Saturday!< /text>
